Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Intermarriage Between Whites and Blacks 238

— Meng Ruo

A large part of the world's disputes stem from racial differences. If all the people in this world were of the same race, they would definitely be more polite to each other, and there would not be as many conflicts as there are now. Who knew that the God who created the universe would be so unfair, dividing the humans distributed across the five continents into five races: yellow, white, black, red, and brown, giving each race a different color in their skin pigment. This makes things difficult. There is a type of person who thinks they were specially made by God, that they are God's chosen people, and the most superior members of humanity. They not only think this way themselves, but also force those of different races to be inferior races, saying that you were made by God with the worst materials. Naturally, the superior and inferior races in the world are all assigned and settled.

Yesterday, I happened to see a very interesting news item in the newspaper, saying that after returning from South Africa, George Bernard Shaw believed that the white birth rate was low, and that they would not be able to maintain their advantage in South Africa in the future. Therefore, he advocated that whites and blacks should intermarry. Shaw's proposal was obviously to maintain the white's advantage in South Africa, and not to break down the concept of racial difference. Unexpectedly, this sentence caused astonishment among all Germans. Germans are a white race, which is what I mentioned earlier: the superior race that considers itself to be God's chosen people. And the black race? They are an inferior race. Shaw wants the superior white race to intermarry with the inferior black race, which cannot but cause astonishment among the German people. However, Professor K. Eyssel, the South African ambassador to Germany, is a famous racial scholar, and he strongly disagrees with this view. He believes that Shaw's words are irresponsible remarks from a playwright. Not only does the South African government not think this way, but all white people in South Africa want to maintain the purity of their race, and believe that whites will be able to reproduce and continue in South Africa, and that white culture is European culture, which is a culture that cannot be compromised.

After all, Professor Eyssel is a famous racial scholar, so he has this kind of opinion. As for George Bernard Shaw, he is just a playwright who can only spout some irresponsible words.

A Visit to the Shanghai Free Circulating Library 239

— Qi Shui

The hardship of work turns us into foolish silkworms:

We feel the hunger for knowledge more than bread!

This is what the Shanghai Free Circulating Library said in its recent founding statement.

The name Shanghai Free Circulating Library must be very unfamiliar to readers. That's right, this is what a few young people recently, as they said in their origin, deeply felt the hunger for knowledge in their work, and even more felt that many out-of-school youths in society, all people at work, deeply felt the hunger for knowledge. Therefore, they held this Make their own knowledge can be somewhat satisfied, and to make the general public who are also hungry for knowledge and in pursuit of some satisfaction, holding such a aspiration—this aspiration is said to be very small, but also very grand—established this voluntary circulating library.

Thanks to a friend's introduction, I recently had this

Page 18

opportunity to visit the circulating library run by several enthusiastic young people.

I was deeply moved by the enthusiasm and perseverance of these young people in serving society. Therefore, I have to write down some of the thoughts I gained after the visit here to introduce the library and the general readers. I firmly believe that this is not an unnecessary task. In this society, the support for this library? I think it is naturally our responsibility.

The location of this library is at No. 13 Yangci Lane, Yuezhou Road (terminus of the 18th Road trolleybus) in this city. The founders are Yao Jun and several other young people who are enthusiastic about social service. They all have their own occupations, but they can better spend half of their spare time running this library. This library has only been established for nearly a month now, but the number of readers has already reached two hundred and sixty-seventy, and dozens of people come to the library to read every day. This library is completely voluntary, and readers do not have to pay any price to borrow books. There are currently about three thousand books, which are not complete, but there are some in all categories. According to Yao Jun, the readers are mostly nearby senior primary school students, accounting for about 40%, followed by small shop employees, and then workers and housewives in nearby factories. Yao Jun also said that the reason why so many nearby senior primary school students come to the library to borrow books is because these schools only know how to collect tuition fees and do not pay attention to the library facilities of the school. Secondly, whether modern education is beneficial to the general youth is also a problem. Therefore, these young people in the strong pursuit of knowledge have no choice but to warmly approach this small and simple library. This opinion is very accurate. From this, we can also see how urgently the general libraries in society, similar to this library, are needed by the general public who seek knowledge.

Secondly, there is the question of books. Because their strength is limited, most of the books are donated. However, according to their experience, it is very difficult to donate books to people of status in the general society. On the contrary, general unfamiliar readers are their most enthusiastic book donors. Here, it can also be seen that this library, on the one hand, serves the society, and on the other hand, is based on the knowledge-seeking masses of the society.

The position occupied by this library is only a small room, but their enthusiasm and expectations for the future are very far-reaching. I hope that the general readers in society can give it the greatest support. We must remember:

Helping the development of this library is also helping the development of our own knowledge!

Village Welcoming Drums 240

— Ke Ming

The strong sun shines on the cracked yellow earth day after day, and the weather gets hotter day by day. The tender rice stalks are scorched hot, as if they have been fried dry. The hearts of the farmers are also anxiously roasted like in boiling oil. After the Dragon Boat Festival (this Dragon Boat Festival can no longer be compared with the past, people's minds are all transformed into finding food to fill their stomachs, and no one remembers this festival anymore.), the weather is still so dry, but the rice's need for water is becoming more and more urgent. The air in the village is also becoming tense. In the fields, by the streams, on the winch-like water scoops, and in the small teahouses in the town, anxious faces and sighs can be found everywhere: "Last year was a year of famine, and the villagers have already lost most of their lives, and they still have to dig sweet potatoes to eat at the end of autumn. If this year is another drought, if this year is another famine, if there is no rain in the next few days..." Thinking, when facing the perilous scene, is feeble. When I think of the experience of being hungry for a year, it's like throwing a stone into my heart, pressing down heavily, and I no longer have the courage to think about it.

It can be said that the weather is really good. The strong sun shines continuously for the whole month, roasting like a roast. By the end of May, people have become dizzy, and even a short cloth shirt with a bare chest cannot be worn. People are full of fear and resentment, "Even the sky is working against people!" Thinking so, there is no strength to work in the fields, and the heart is half cold. People come back from the fields at dusk, walk past the water scoop, and glared at it fiercely, as if saying, "You will soon be needed, and you will soon be used to fight against God." Last year, when it was dry, more than a dozen families in the village used foreign pumps to save part of the fields, but this year, people are already "nine out of ten empty," and even sowing in the spring was a reluctant risk. Who can afford to use foreign pumps? There are still...

Nothing is happening. We, who are called "outsiders," spend four copper coins on a teahouse (the town's "tiger stove"), and someone will tell you about the situation in the fields. In fact, this is not bad; in recent years, whether it is farming or doing small business, there are many unspeakable hardships; it is originally a difficult year, and everything is not going well, which is also an understandable situation that can be expected!

(An old man, with wrinkles like messy grass piled on his forehead, and a thin, dark face, muttering like chanting a terrible curse, uttering unclear syllables:

"Farmland? It's really useless! Staying is also waiting to die. I'm old, if I were still young. Like you young men, I would have gone out with you to the north and south. Anyway, it's difficult to do anything these days. Wandering out, maybe you can wander out a situation, at least you can see more of the world! People can't even get enough to eat, what are you talking about ease, floating like a duck, isn't it good?")

The atmosphere of survival, wandering, and medieval pirates has also fallen on this small village. Hunger has pushed these self-sufficient, cowardly, narrow, and simple people out of the old village, and has given them a novel lesson from the outside world, a wonderful lesson like a kaleidoscope.

(The strong sun is still fiercely shining, and everyone's heart is anxious: but, some younger, curious, and strong young men are increasingly interested in wandering: "Maybe the outside world is a better-looking one?")

In this way, there are already fewer young people doing fieldwork in the village this year—they are bravely throwing themselves into the outside world to find life two: and what fills the village is an atmosphere of sighing in the twilight of life.

Night Walk 241

— Hua Zhi

The city's nights are no different from its days; it's no exaggeration to call it a "city that never sleeps." It has become a habit for urban dwellers to return home at midnight. When one entrusts one's weary body to a rickshaw, the short journey feels like a pardon for a criminal. Leaning back in the carriage, legs propped up, free and natural, listening to the sound of the rickshaw puller's footsteps hitting the asphalt, a kind of passionate sound; or sometimes pulling over a road under construction, the carriage body swaying slightly like a pendulum, if I weren't constantly worried about a somersault when stopping, I could sleep soundly like a lazy pig; however, I was often woken up by the rickshaw puller. For years, I have been living a mechanical life. It is said that the city's nights are mysterious, but I have never really understood its true nature. It doesn't feel familiar to me, but it inexplicably grows.

The day before the Dragon Boat Festival, an old classmate from middle school invited me to his new home in Jiangwan. On the phone, he told me that he had spent a lot of time inviting more than a dozen old friends from our classroom at the time, and that this rare gathering should be enjoyed to the fullest.

Because I am a husband and have the burden of a family, I am often entangled in many unwilling things during people's joyous festivals; by the time I had dealt with all the difficulties, it was already evening.

For this rare gathering, I mustered the greatest courage and took a tram to Tiantong'an Station. Going to Jiangwan was not the first time. The small train gave me a good impression. The seats were comfortable and the journey was short. If you leaned against the window, looking at the clusters of green trees, and unintentionally eavesdropped on the trivial daily conversations of the villagers, the worries and hatred accumulated in your heart would disappear without a trace, like catkins blown by the light breeze of early summer.

As I got on the train, a drizzle suddenly started to fall. Before I could finish a cigarette, it intensified, and by the time I arrived at Jiangwan Station, white lines of rain were cascading down from the eaves. Almost everyone on the train had not brought rain gear, so they rushed out of the station to hail rickshaws. But when I was surrounded by a group of rickshaw pullers, I almost laughed. What was my friend's address? Yes, I had been to Jiangwan more than once, and because I was familiar with the route, I had never asked for the street name or address. In a desperate situation, I grabbed a rickshaw puller and told him, as if guessing a riddle, that I had to pass several bridges, those bridges were marked with six or eight tons of load, and turn left on the left side of a house destroyed by artillery fire. The rickshaw puller nodded repeatedly. He said that was called what place. I was already unable to listen to him. I hid in the carriage and urged him to pull faster, because the street lights at the station were turned off after the train left.

My body was full of rain. I drove past many roads in a daze. The rickshaw puller stopped the car beside a small bridge. I raised my disappointed eyes, and there was not even a trace of my friend's house in the vicinity. The two of us stood in the rain, guessing charades again.

After being resolutely rejected by the rickshaw puller, I could only grope my way alone. At this time, there was not a single passerby, and the street lights were so dim. I could not distinguish east, west, south, or north. Like a water ghost, I walked to a bridge marked with eight tons, carefully guessing the houses on both sides, as if my friend's house was nearby; but the most accurate marker – a collapsed house – was missing. I peered at the shops with closed doors, and in front of a white wooden door hung an advertisement for "×× Construction Company承造." This was originally the address of the collapsed house, and the place where I had just stopped was only a few steps away. I knocked on my friend's door, laughing to myself. They were surprised that I hadn't broken my promise as they had expected. At this night's gathering, everyone roused the naivety of when they boasted shamelessly in the past, the naivety that would never return!

Perhaps this is a rare night walk in the history of my life?

She is willing to teach any subject except music and physical education, and can handle the rest. Treatment requires board and lodging, and a monthly salary of 30 to 40 yuan. If you want to try her out, please send a letter to Mr. Zhou, No. 101, Xueyuan Road, Chengnan.

News 244

The 12th issue of Dianyin Weekly was published today. The content now includes three new sections: "Radio," "Hollywood," and "Metropolitan Scenery." The content and text are exceptionally wonderful, and there is an accurate joint program schedule for radio stations. Each copy sells for six copper coins. All newsstands sell it. For a sample copy with postage, please send half a cent to the headquarters at No. 48, Juqing Lane, Xinzha Road, Shanghai. Subscription for the whole year, including postage, is 1 yuan and 20 cents. The Chinese Broadcasting Special Issue has been well received by all walks of life and sells widely after its publication. The magazine contains Suzhou ballad openings, new songs, photos of singers, Shanghai opera scripts, Suzhou difficult lyrics, etc. The original price was 40 cents of ocean. Now, the Rose Singing Troupe, in order to thank the audience, is offering a 50% discount to those who send a letter to the Rose Troupe to purchase it, selling it for 20 cents of ocean.

Movie News

Yuan Meiyun's Yearning for Spring 245

Some describe Yuan Meiyun's liveliness, saying she is like a little bird on a spring branch, others describe her beauty, saying she is like the bright stars and moon in the night, the gorgeous colorful clouds in the sky at sunset.

Indeed: Meiyun's liveliness is like a little bird, Meiyun's beauty is like stars and moon, like colorful clouds.

Meiyun is very young, just a girl in her youth, a girl who needs love to comfort her, but Meiyun has never shown any expression of love, although she has declared that she does not need love, but that is precisely the exposure of her ambition, she is now really a girl who needs love to comfort her, if you don't believe it, then you can prove it from a love song she sang in the sound film "Song of Triumph" directed by Wan Cang under Yi Hua's production, she sings like this: "The weather in June Jiangnan is clear, my sister goes to pick water chestnuts in the pond, the water chestnut tips prick the hand, the scorching sun shines on people, Oh God!, I have never seen it not raining during the plum rain season, I have never seen an eighteen-year-old girl not marrying, thinking of youth in the water chestnut mirror".

When Meiyun sang like this, her younger brother Jiusheng - played by Liu Li - shamed her and said: "Sister, aren't you afraid of being embarrassed?"

"Little devil, you are so bad." Meiyun's face turned as red as the sunset glow.

Yuan Meiyun yearns for spring, in the sound film "Song of Triumph" directed by Bu Wancang.

Tianyi Special Dispatch 246

Formation of a Singing Team

In Tianyi's new sound film "Mother," there is a scene of studying abroad, which requires dozens of male and female students to sing the "Farewell Song." For this reason, Tianyi formed a singing team. One of the hosts is Miss Shao Suxia, who studies music at the Shanghai Art College, and the other is Miss Ding Zhi of the Lianhua Vocal Music Troupe. The other team members are male and female students from Daxia, Fudan and other schools. They are now stepping up their practice every day.

Joining of New Talents

The lack of new talents is the most important thing felt in the current film circle. Tianyi Company also needs new talents just like other companies, so Tianyi is also cultivating new talents.

Recently, two new talents have joined, one is "Miss Beiping" Bai Fen, and the other is "Miss Tianjin" Xu Lina. Both of them speak standard Mandarin, which is naturally what we need for filming sound films. What their future holds will depend on their own efforts.

Wang Bin's "Sea Burial"

The script for "Sea Burial," the debut work written and directed by the newly promoted director Wang Bin, has been formally approved after the initial review, and preparations are now being made for the separation of scenes, etc. The start of filming is not far away.

Wang Bin's "Sea Burial" is undoubtedly a powerful, rough-lined script. It is said that the play entirely depicts the struggling life of fishermen, and the intention is extremely great and sublime.

Mingyue Society Will Publicly Perform "Peanuts" Song and Dance Drama 247

The new four-act song and dance drama "Peanuts" by Mingyue Society has a tragic and enthusiastic content, and is both sad and humorous. After half a year of rehearsal time, it has now been completed. In order to seek perfection in technology, it is still constantly rehearsing every day. Now it has responded to the invitation of a large Shanghai theater and decided to stage it at the end of this month, or at the latest at the beginning of next month. When this news reached the people who were fans of song and dance, they of course eagerly awaited the debut of "Mingyue Society." Chinese song and dance has reached a state of exhaustion, and only Mingyue is left as a slightly sound song and dance group in Shanghai. Their past achievements have not disappointed the audience. Now we are looking forward to them giving us satisfactory results. On the left is a scene from the performance by Bai Hong and Li Mingjian.
